烏發攝影探險隊長訪問（上） 277

— 馨甫

在烏發攝影探險隊隊長烏利克叔爾次博士Ｄr·Ulrich　K·T·Ｓchulz從北歐回到柏林的第三天，有一位記者到烏發公司去訪問他·一脚跨進了博士的辦事室，看上去，就很像一間科學家或是探險家的研究室·他們就在這樣一個地方，毫不客氣的開談起來：

「你要看我嗎？好，那末就請你把要問我的話說出來吧！」

「請你告訴我，在我進來以前，你正在想着什麽？」

「你想！一個離開柏林五個月，剛從北歐工作回來的我：除掉那在北歐所拍的片子和那些地方的人情風俗外我還會想着什麽别的事情呢？相信我，那北方的物物事事，都和這裏不同的，我早就有「到北歐去」的心思了，却被那北歐的嚴寒天氣，屢次挫折了我的勇氣，但是現在終於被我達到目的了·這次多謝那精良的器械，使得我們拍了許多很有價值的影片·我們不僅在水面上和水底下去攝取景物：並且還駕着飛機到空中去攝取。一萬五千尺高，是算不了一回事的·那挪威峽江的海口，横互大陸二百六十英里·我們除坐着飛機渡過外，還曾坐着帆船，在斷巖絶壁的夾岸中，來來往往·

取魚羣在靜水中産卵的情形·」

「你願把這一次最富有興趣的經歷告訴我嗎？」

「十分願意，在峽江的靠岸上，樹着許多花兒開得正盛的樹木·你想這樣美麗的樹木，在它的背面，是懸崖斷壁和白雪，在它的前面，是一片汪洋大海·這是多麽有趣的天然美景呢！所以，我們在飛渡峽江的時候，曾用反光攝影法去攝取了很多的奇景·」

「什麽呌反光攝影法，可否解釋給我聽嗎？」

「平常的攝影。是和太陽光相對的·這樣好呌那目的物，受着陽光，而反射出光線來；但是我們攝影，是反對着太陽光的·這種方法·發明未久，不但便利，且以前不能攝取的奇景，現在都能夠攝取了：像我們這次所攝取的急流瀑布的美景，都是採用這種法子的·（未完）

觀衆意見

關於「都會的早晨」的幾篇來稿 278

（一）牠是偉大的成功 279

— 嚴繼陵

在意識方面，它也獲得了偉大成功。它並没有小資産階級幻滅的空想，它指示了大衆光明的前途。它告訴了勞苦的大衆：什麽都不要怕，也不要受富人虚僞的憐憫，也不要貪圖一己的亨受：只有在艱苦壓迫的生活之下，奮力的爭扎，男敢的給予壓迫者以無情的，殘酷的捶擊，才是勞苦大衆的出路。

表演方面，高占非和王人美都非常有力。袁叢美的反派，確是老手。唐槐秋在初出現的時候，太覺呆板，以後還不差。其餘如王桂林，劉繼羣都很可以。扮幼年許蘭光的嚴朶匀，很有表演的天才，是一個可造的孩子。

（二）他亦說劇情偉大 280

— 馮瑛

劇本的眞諦，我們是值得欽佩的，他處處顯示出勞工的神聖，高尙，但在畸形社會下的中國，非但貧富的階級懸殊，而且社會的經濟，也分配太不均衡，以致造成神聖，高尙的勞工們，每天勞働所得的酬報，僅能勉强地維持個人的生活，而那些不事生産的資本家，很安舒地過着不勞而獲的生活，都會的早晨一片，是爲大衆的神聖，高尙的勞工們作有力的呐喊，同時在另一方面，無疑地，給時代的人們以偉大的啓示。

至於演員方面，高占非那樣的剛毅堅强的深刻表演，使吾感發無限的同情，王人美的天眞漫爛，祗覺得她可愛極了，王桂林的慈父愛子，看了簡直　人淚下。

總之，該片在表演，意義的種種方面，已獲得極大的成功，可是在情節方面，似乎有點覺得不大緊凑。

「萬花獻媚」是一部熱的歌舞鉅片由埃第康泰主演今日開映於光陸蘭心大戲院。

（三）但有矛盾欠缺之處 281

— 椀

沉浸在黑暗都市裏頭的人們，苦悶極了！誰不憬幢着有一線晨光之到來，照我們走上光明之路呢？因此「都市的早晨」就應着時代的要求，而出映了。牠和「城市之夜」正是銜接一氣的片子；劇情，表演，攝影，一切的一切，都有異曲同工之妙。不過「城市之夜」的力量，比較還要深刻一點！這張片子也算是聨華的成功作。不過細看起來，裏頭還有不少的漏洞

第一，是許多演員，不會走路。動步太快，顯出太怱遽的樣子。

第二，是工人拉車子的時候，完全不用力，顯著是在拍戲。

第三，農村裏頭的小三子，打諢的地方，嫌多一點。

這些是表演的缺點；還有劇情方面，亦有矛盾糢糊之處。

茅盾的小說「子夜」將攝電影 282

— 趙鵬

洪深田漢建議

聨華公司採用

斯文學作家沈從文（茅盾）近作的長篇小說「子夜一，描寫深刻，寓意精深，極得社會人士之熱烈歡迎，電影戲劇界鉅子洪深田漢等，特向聨華公司建議，主張將沈氏的長篇小說「子夜」改編爲電影劇本，業已得聨華公司導演蔡楚生同意，惟沈氏欲求保持其作品眞面目起見，特要求當局，編成劇本不能改變作者的本旨，主角演員，須對戲劇文藝有修養者擔任；關於心理描寫之處，由作者親自導演，俾體貼入微，公司當局，深韙其意，刻正在計劃一切，一俟就緒，即將拍攝云。

（四）推崇高袁的幾句話 283

— 沈千里

高占非主演的片子，總算我領敎了不少了。然而能夠差强人意的，就不多見。「粉紅色的夢」和開映未久的「天明」，在一部份的人或者認爲是他的成功；我却以爲那還祗登堂而未入室，「都會的早晨」公映了以後，才算告訴了我們他已經升進藝術之階，得窺堂奥了。在這裏他是無暇可擊。不過我同時發現了他這次的成功，劇本却給了他不少的助力。否則繼有表演的天才，也就等於「英雄無用武之地」。

袁叢美我可以不必說了，祇要把蔡楚生的話借用一次就行；「……在他的純潔的生活中，罪惡是無從闖入的，但由於他的想像和創造，事實上已造成他在銀幕上唯一的反派明星的地位。……並且要感謝他在「都會的早晨」：在反面上增加了不少的力量。」誠然，想像和創造，這在每個明星的成功上是不可少的要素，不僅袁叢美個人就應當如此。

（五）年號應加注意 284

— 黃影呆

全劇的取材，完全以暗示着人們以遺産的流毒和勞工的神聖使銀幕下的觀衆，得以認識那人生的眞義，和無的放矢，一意胡閙的劇本當然有不同樣的結果，和不同樣的功效。我們自然不能不說這劇本的成功！

演員方面，人材是很平均謬疵的地方很少而尤其使得我們贊美的便是王人美的蘭兒，她一種活潑天眞的情狀演來恰恰是適合於一個村姑的身分，我們很希望聨華的導演們能抓住她的個性，使她能發展她的演劇天才。

不過從我的主觀上說來，都會的早晨呢，全劇的序幕，覺得還有些疏鬆而不能到達十分緊張的境地，至於表示時間的前進的年期我覺得中國的影片，應當用民國×年而不必去用一九一九丨丨一九三三等字幕來表示，因爲我們中國也自有固有的年號，又何必去借用西曆呢？不知讀者以爲何如？

黃耐霜創辦歌舞研究團 285

快樂影　公司第二部出品「拚命」充當女主角的黃耐霜，他本來在曁南公司充當基本演員，最近的出品「爲國爭光」亦是黃擔任主角。現因二片均將攝竣，於是想在空暇時間創辦一個歌舞團，現在聽說已在招集團員，並定名爲耐霜歌舞研究團，因此我想不久的將來或者能夠在舞臺上同她們見面呢！

一五里計劃」失敗 286

— 雲君

最近在好萊塢老鄉村中發生一宗新奇的事件，就是行將六十五歲的英籍老明星喬治亞立斯的「五里計劃」，就是每天早上他要走五英里路。

在卡休恩加（Cahueng）道上，老當益壯的亞立斯先生一步一步的向前踱着。他的汽車和他的汽車夫在後面跟著。

當亞立斯先生覺得有一點兒步履維艱的時候，他就自動他走向汽車，躍進車中。結果所謂五英里的步行只走了五分之一，其餘的四英里是由亞立斯的汽車載着走的。心有餘而力不足，因此轟動一時的「五里計劃」宣告失敗了。

“Ｃavalcade”（忠魂錄）攝製經過記 287

— 凛

美國福斯公司新攝鉅片名Ｃavalcade者，原書出諸英國名小說作家諾爾老華德氏Ｎoel　Coward手筆，英倫三島，傳誦一時，視爲國家光榮之傑構。美國福斯公司以鉅欵向作者購得影片攝製權，加以　珞之攝製。英國全國輿論爲之譁然，指老華德此舉爲辱國之行爲。今福斯公司已費數百萬金錢將此片攝製完成。大西洋兩岸，俱爲之轟動，價值之偉，可想而知矣。茲擬將此劇本事，節譯充實申報電影刋。惟此片攝製之先，遺自逸事，未經人道者尚夥，茲特掇要述之，以作譯文之先導焉。

此書之大旨，歷述二十世紀初葉以來，英國所受戰禍之慘烈，與夫某巨宦（書中之主人翁）家室蕩析流離之苦，而以十九世紀末葉維多利亞后時代之承平景象爲對照，其中頗多情感動人之處。作者之以攝影權售諸好萊塢，原非圖博厚利。今福斯公司片成，作者之心，庶可告無愧於英倫之國人，蓋此種偉大之財力，爲攝製此片，幾將一九零零年全倫敦一切名勝遷植好萊塢，使當年遺老游其地者，幾疑疑三十年前之故都，往往有爲之感泣不成聲者，可知佈置之精偉矣。

此書之攝影權，旣由考華德氏售諸好萊塢而激起英倫人士之反響後，福斯公司爲見好英人及不失英倫本色起見，决定全劇演員，悉用英人，凡非在倫敦生長而在倫敦受敎育者，一槪不得充演員。卽導演攝影師燈光師等亦槪以英人充之。因此之故，福斯女主角如安哈定，愛琳童　伊朋莎蘭第等，俱不能入選，而以新自英倫來美之蒂安娜嬝（Ｄlana　Ｗypyard）充之。福斯名導演鮑才琪，亦祇可於籌備攝製之中參與工作，而正導演則聰英人佛蘭克勞合（Ｆrand　Lloyd）充之。並延英下議院員瑞金諾勃克雷（Ｒeginld　Berkoy）爲影戲劇本編輯員。

攝製表演之全部人員旣須以英籍人充之，福斯公司感覺美國境内，英籍人才之缺乏。遂不得不派遺專員赴倫敦，就該劇之舞　演員中物色之。幾經愼重　選，復得男女演員數人。然其中亦有中途發生困難，出乎公司意料之外者。如劇中之孩童演員，本己　得相當人才，合同亦已訂立，不意於登舟赴美之際，突爲英移民當局所禁阻，蓋據英律有「童子十四齡以下者不得出國表演謀利」之一條。公司受此阻碍，遂不　不更變計劃，在美境英人家庭中物色　角焉。（未完）

1933.03.29

League of Nations and International Reactions 1

League of Nations Advisory Committee Meeting Yesterday

Japanese Council Seat Vacancy Sparks Competition

(Geneva) Japan's notification of withdrawal from the League of Nations has been transmitted by telegraph to League of Nations Secretary-General Drummond at 3:10 PM today. The Secretariat immediately replied to the Japanese Foreign Minister and promptly forwarded the Japanese telegram along with the League of Nations' reply to all member states of the League of Nations. (Havas dispatch, 27th)

(London) Japan's withdrawal from the League of Nations will only become effective after two years. However, several national leaders are already considering reorganizing the Administrative Council after Japan's withdrawal from its permanent seat. Smaller nations are increasingly resentful of the Administrative Council's control, especially in handling the Sino-Japanese dispute and the disarmament conference. Recently, such ominous sentiments have shown signs of escalating into open rebellion. Therefore, political observers do not consider the movement to reform the Administrative Council or change the election system to be strange. Today, the Evening Standard anticipates internal turmoil within the League of Nations, similar to what happened before Germany joined the League in 1926. The newspaper believes that the Little Entente countries have long considered themselves great powers and will eventually demand to fill the seat vacated by Japan. France, Poland, and some smaller nations will undoubtedly support them, but Italy, Germany, and other countries opposed to the French faction will resist this as well. Therefore, the League of Nations Administrative Council may soon become the focus of conflicting European fears and ambitions. (Reuters dispatch, 27th)

(Geneva) Representatives of major powers and some smaller nations have slightly differing opinions on whether it is beneficial to convene a 21-member Advisory Committee meeting under the current circumstances. From the perspective of major powers, it is questionable whether the committee can discuss Japan's withdrawal from the League of Nations and whether the US representative's attendance at this meeting will exceed the scope of authority. However, Advisory Committee Chairman Lange decided to take action as before before the representatives leave for the Easter holiday. Therefore, a meeting was scheduled for 5:30 PM today. (Reuters dispatch, 28th)

Mandated Islands Issue 2

(London) In the House of Commons today, Conservative Party member Baxter inquired about the proper handling of mandated territories under the control of a League of Nations member that withdraws from the League. Under-Secretary Eden replied that the British government is considering the issue, but because major powers have not yet discussed it, the British government cannot express its position at this time. (Reuters dispatch, 27th)

(New York) The State Department believes that Japan's withdrawal from the League of Nations was expected. The United States will not change its policies towards Japan and the League of Nations as a result. The US government is committed to maintaining world peace and will continue to cooperate closely with the League of Nations while independently resolving the Far Eastern issue. The US representative will follow the State Department's reply to the League of Nations on March 13, participating in the Advisory Committee organized by the League of Nations to monitor the Far Eastern issue. The US authorities are extremely concerned about the issue of Japanese-mandated islands in the Pacific, especially within naval circles, because if Japan and the United States come into conflict, these islands will be of great strategic importance. American newspapers have repeatedly criticized Japan for building fortifications in the Caroline Islands. In January of this year, the Director of the Far Eastern Division of the State Department stated that the mandate system originated from the European War. Although the United States is not a member of the League of Nations, it was a participating party in the war, and therefore has the right to participate in all views and decisions regarding the mandate territories. (Havas dispatch, 27th)

(Berlin) Recently, Japanese newspapers reported that the Japanese and German governments began consultations on the 4th of this month regarding the continuation of the administration of the former German colonies in the Pacific after Japan's withdrawal from the League of Nations. The Berlin government authority stated today that this is not the case. Therefore, all German opinions and actions related to this issue propagated by the Japanese side are unfounded fabrications. Furthermore, Germany's view on this issue remains the same as announced a few days ago, without any changes. (National Telegraph, 27th)

(Berlin) The news reported in Japanese newspapers regarding the administration of the Caroline Islands, claiming it was stated to a Japanese interviewer by National Socialist Party member Rosenberg, is now refuted by the National Socialist Party's official newspaper, which states that Rosenberg has not met with any Japanese interviewers. (National Telegraph, 27th)

Fierce Enemy Attacks at Jielingkou 3

Heavy Fighting on the Left Flank of Shimenzhai

Scouts in Contact on the Shihe Front

Enemy Retreats from Xifengkou Face Towards Kuancheng

Japanese Troops Reinforce for Second Phase of Operations

Enemy Planes Bombard Jiumentou and Shimenzhai

(Beiping) On the Jielingkou front, the main force of the enemy's 10th Division has been launching fierce attacks for days. As of this morning, fierce fighting is still ongoing in the area. The Japanese army plans to capture Jielingkou to cut off the connection between our forces at Shihe and Lengkou. (Special dispatch, 28th)

(Lezhou) Haiyang reports by telephone on the evening of the 28th that on the left flank of Shimenzhai, Yao Shi's [unclear characters] regiment's [unclear character] battalion has made contact with the enemy's advancing troops and is engaged in fierce fighting. On the same evening, on the right flank of Shihe, at Huimazhai, about a hundred enemy soldiers attacked our Dongfengdingshan position but were repelled by our defending soldiers. (Special dispatch, morning of the 29th)

(Beiping) The enemy at Jielingkou, on the 27th, resumed bombing with formations of aircraft, covering their infantry's advance. Our troops showed no fear, remaining hidden in the trenches. When the artillery fire lessened and the infantry approached, they suddenly opened fire, killing many enemies. Subsequently, a certain regiment took the opportunity to launch an attack, and the other units, hearing the news, rose up and leaped out of the trenches to launch a counterattack. The enemy suffered a major defeat, fleeing in disarray. Our troops pursued for five or six li, but withdrew to their original positions to defend them as it was getting late. (Special dispatch, 28th)

(Beiping) After the Japanese army failed to attack Xifengkou and Luowenyu, they are deploying the 14th Division for reinforcements, preparing for the second phase of operations. Commander of the Kwantung Army, Muto Nobuyoshi, is currently planning everything in Chengde. Currently, the focus of the war has shifted to the Shihe and Gubeikou lines. The Japanese army at Shihe is actively moving, and troops have also been increased at Jiumentou. In order to concentrate its forces, our army has deployed solid positions along the Le County and Changli lines. There have been constant scouting clashes on the Shihe front for the past two days. (Special dispatch, 28th)

(Lezhou) The Japanese army has changed its strategy and is still attempting to attack Le Eastern from the Jiumentou and Qinyu area. There are reports of an impending attack. The Shihe front line has been tense for days. On the 26th, scouts even made contact. The enemy's invading troops are using puppet troops as the vanguard. Jin Dianchen and Zhang Ziming, two traitors, have arrived in Yu. The former pacification area has opened to about 10,000 infantry and cavalry of the traitor Zhang Hai-peng's forces, and they have arrived in Suizhong. Li Jichun and Zhao Lei's forces, about two thousand men, have arrived in the northwest of Shimenzhai. Traitor Zheng's son has established the headquarters of the puppet National Salvation Army in Zhuchao Ying. (Special dispatch, 28th)

(Beiping) The Shihe front line is tense. Bai Fengxiang returned to Shunde this morning to defend it. (Special dispatch, 28th)

(Tianjin) The Japanese army has changed its strategy and is attempting to attack the Le Eastern Shihe front line from the Qinyu Jiumentou area using puppet troops. There was scout contact on the 26th. The enemy troops in the Yu area have been moving very actively for days. Jin Dingchen and Zhang Ziming, two traitors, have arrived in Yu. Traitor Xiao Xu's son Yanxiang has established the headquarters of the puppet National Salvation Army in Zhuchao Ying. About 10,000 infantry and cavalry of the traitor Zhang Hai-peng's forces have arrived in the Sui Zhong vanguard area. (Special dispatch, 28th)

(Beiping) More than three thousand traitor troops have departed from Yuguan and are advancing towards the Jiumentou and Shihe lines. Zhang Hai-peng's son, Zhang Ziming, organized a headquarters in Daxi Guan after arriving in Yuguan yesterday. There are still more than five thousand traitor troops who will arrive from Suizhong in a continuous stream in the coming days. Once the enemy's preparations are complete, they will attack the Shihe line. (Special dispatch, 28th)

(Beiping) Yesterday afternoon, a little after 5:00 PM, three enemy aircraft reconnoitered and bombed the area of Jiumentou, Shimenzhai, Hanzhuang, and Haiyang Town. The extent of the damage is unknown. (Special dispatch, 28th)

(Beiping) Two more enemy warships have arrived in the sea off Qin Island, bringing the total to seven. A small number of marines landed and transported food. After nightfall, the lights of the ships would occasionally shine towards our Shihe line. Yesterday, more than 300 traitor troops attacked our troops at Shimenzhai, but they were repelled. At 1:00 AM this morning, they attacked our troops again, with three tanks providing cover. Our defending soldiers repelled the enemy tanks with direct-fire artillery. The Japanese and traitor troops suffered more than a dozen casualties, and the enemy retreated towards the Shizuizi area. (Special dispatch, 28th)

Battle Situation on the Qing Shankou Front 4

(Beiping) Due to transportation obstructions in the Qing Shankou area for days, news of the war has been quiet. Today, a senior officer of Wan Biao Miao's division arrived in Ping and said that on the 16th, more than 300 enemies bypassed to Guo Jiazhangziling Zhuang. A certain regiment of our army was bombed to death by enemy aircraft. Fortunately, a certain regiment reinforced and fought hard, regaining the original position, killing more than 200 enemies. However, a certain regiment only had five companies left. Both sides suffered heavy losses. On the morning of the 23rd, more than 500 enemy infantry attacked Jielingkou and were repelled. Immediately after, they launched a joint infantry and artillery attack on a certain regiment position of our Miao Division. After resisting with all their might for two days and nights, the enemy failed and retreated. Because the enemy reinforced several times, our army transferred a certain regiment of Sun Division to reinforce. From the early morning to noon of the 24th, the enemy, with more than 20 aircraft in formation, more than 10 artillery pieces, and more than 1,000 infantry, jointly attacked our facing position. Division Commander Miao retreated to defend the Ma Fang line because the ratio of soldiers was too different. On the evening of the 24th, a certain regimental commander of the Sun Division led a certain battalion to detour to the right flank to assist the Miao Division, restoring the original position, killing hundreds of enemies and capturing a lot of enemy guns and baggage. At noon on the 25th, a certain regiment of the Sun Division, which detoured behind the enemy, encountered more than 100 enemy ammunition and supply vehicles and more than 100 puppet Japanese enemy soldiers at Caojiadian. They were surrounded by our army and wiped out. (Special dispatch, 27th)

(Beiping) Qin Island telegram states that Qin Island and Shihe are both safe and Shimenzhai is undamaged, firmly defended by Jin Tuan. A few days ago, Yuguan increased Japanese soldiers by more than 200, and more than 100 puppet troops came from Suizhong, with three mountain cannons, stationed near Dongluocheng. The enemy often reconnoiters our Shihe position, and communicates with lights on the Yuguan city wall at night. (Special dispatch, 28th)

(Beiping) On the Luowenyu front, there have only been small clashes recently. The enemy's newly arrived troops, after being defeated at Banbishan, have now retreated to the Shouwangmu area, about seventy or eighty li from Luowenyu. Our cavalry is tracking, scouting, and pursuing them. The enemy is extremely brutal in harassing the villagers in the rear, forcibly pulling civilians every day to carry the wounded. Those who disobey are killed. (Special dispatch, 28th)

(Beiping) At about 4:00 PM on the 27th, the enemy used 400-500 plainclothes troops to sneak attack our Xifengkou area. After our army discovered them, the garrison soldiers did not fire their guns, waiting for them to get closer, and then attacked them fiercely with grenades, followed by slashing with knives. More than 200 enemies were killed, with corpses everywhere. The enemies who continued to advance, seeing the ferocity of our broadsword fighters and grenades, fled in panic. Our side only had 14 soldiers injured. (Special dispatch, 28th)

(Beiping) Zunhua telegram states that on the Xifengkou front, the enemy has withdrawn from Mengziling towards Kuancheng. For days, no enemy aircraft have attacked Xifengkou and Zunhua. It is rumored that when Shao Benliang defected, he burned more than 100 enemy aircraft. The enemy on the Luowenyu front was forced to withdraw to Liuhe after our Liu Ruming Division occupied Banbishan. Our cavalry tracked and pursued them. There was fierce fighting near Liuhe yesterday. The Rehe militia could not bear the enemy's slaughter and often launched night attacks on the enemy camps with broadsword teams on the 23rd. The enemy is extremely afraid of them. (Special dispatch, 28th)

(Beiping) Song Zheyuan told Quan Shaowu, a representative of the support association, that according to reports from the front, the Japanese army at Luowenyu retreated from Banbishan on the 25th and has now retreated to a place ninety li away from Luowenyu. The Japanese army at Xifengkou retreated to Mengziling on the 25th and is constructing fortifications. They retreated again on the 26th and have passed Kuancheng. As for the reasons for the retreat, one is that the Japanese army's military discipline is too bad, harassing everywhere, and the people often come out to attack at night, and the other is that our army is putting great pressure on them. (Special dispatch, 28th)

(Jinzhou) [Unclear characters] Brigade on the Lengkou front has received reinforcements, preventing the Japanese army from advancing. The Japanese [unclear characters] flying team, led by the team leader from Qian Dao, departed from the [unclear characters] airfield at 9:00 AM yesterday, and started fierce bombing from the point where it flew over the Chinese military position. The sound of artillery fire has been deafening yesterday, suppressing the Great Wall of China, and a large fierce battle that has never been seen before has unfolded. (Dentsu telegram, 27th)

(Beiping) On the evening of the 24th, the Japanese army withdrew a field artillery team and about 200 large vehicles from Chifeng, passing through Chaoyang overnight. Also, the Japanese army withdrew many infantry from Lingyuan Xizhoujiazi, all returning to the Beipiao area. The puppet troops are advancing from east to west. (China Alliance telegram, 28th)

Enemy Troops at Yiyuankou Repelled 5

(Tianjin) Three to four hundred enemy troops at Yiyuankou attacked us on the 27th and have been repelled. (Special dispatch, 28th)

Enemy Warships Discovered Outside Xieliangkou 6

(Beiping) On the 27th, one enemy warship and seven sailing ships, each capable of holding a hundred people and able to dock at any time, were discovered two li offshore from Xieliangkou. One Japanese warship is still stationed in the southern sea of Yuguan. (Special dispatch, 28th)

Enemy Attack on Shimenzhai Repelled 7

(Tianjin) More than three hundred enemies attacked Shimenzhai early on the 27th and were repelled. The enemy suffered about forty casualties, while we suffered about ten. (Special dispatch, 28th)

Japanese Side Buys Off Bandits 8

To Disrupt Our Army's Rear

Establishing Secret Organizations in Tianjin

(Beiping) Because the Japanese side has been repeatedly unsuccessful in attacking, they are using money to buy off bandits, giving them two yuan per day, specifically to disrupt our army's rear. They have established secret organizations in Tianjin and have also established a machine in Hankou to supply the communist army with weapons upstream of the Yangtze River. The weapons are transported by Japanese warships to Hankou, Daye, and other places, secretly hidden in Japanese residences, and then secretly transported by small boats on both sides of the Yangtze River. Also, the Japanese army uniforms outside the Great Wall are yellow wool on the outside and gray cloth on the inside. When the two armies are close, they can switch the inside to the outside, attempting to confuse our line of sight. This trick has been seen through by us. (Special dispatch, 28th)

Page 4

Page 5

Current Commentary

Importance of Duolun and Zhangjiakou's Strategic Location 9

Before invading Rehe, Japan claimed that they would only attack Rehe and would not cross the Great Wall in order to ease international criticism and facilitate military operations. Now, Shanhaiguan has already fallen into enemy hands, and all the key passes along the Great Wall, from Gubeikou, Panjiakou, Xifengkou, and Jielingkou to Lengkou and Shimen, are filled with smoke and the sounds of cannons. Even if the outcome is still unknown, the continuous advance of the Japanese army is an obvious and undeniable fact. Furthermore, enemy aircraft frequently fly over the airspace of Zunhua and Miyun to reconnoiter, drop bombs, and wantonly threaten, indicating that the war has extended to the territory of Hebei Province. "Rehe's fall" shows that we did not make full efforts to defend it, which has opened the door for the enemy to covet more. With the repeated loss of natural barriers, it will be even more difficult to resist the enemy in the future. Some believe that the international relations in the Ping [Beiping] and Tianjin areas are complex, and even though Japan is barbaric, it is still aware of its capabilities and dares not act rashly, putting itself in a difficult situation and taking great military risks. Because of this, our country may be able to enjoy a temporary respite. However, we must realize that the situation is evolving and does not allow us to rest for a moment. Yuguan and Rehe are the most serious lessons for our people.

Even worse, now that Japan has seized Rehe, it will be very easy for them to invade North China, and their plot to incite Mongolia has been brewing for a long time. Previously, when Rehe was in our hands, we could indirectly provide supplies to the righteous army, take back Tongliao by taking advantage of the slope of the Shun Qilao Tu mountain range, seize the Siping-Taonan Railway, and take the opportunity to restore the Northeast. Now, the geographical advantage has been shared with the enemy, and they can look down on Northeast China from a high position and spy on Pingjin, while we have become guests and are easily restricted. However, they still have some concerns because Duolun is to their north and Zhangjiakou is around their waist. If our country is determined to get rid of years of bad habits and mobilize the whole country to resist the war, it would not be difficult to recover Rehe. Therefore, the enemy also has the intention of invading Duolun first and then spying on Zhangjiakou. Although this still needs to be proven by facts, judging from Japan's recent actions, it is likely true.

First, Japanese imperialists have been deliberately invading Mongolia for more than a day. Many princes and nobles of various Inner Mongolian leagues have been seduced by them. Now, they are using the name of the puppet state to lure them, and they will certainly be more reckless and expand their invasion area.

Second, Inner and Outer Mongolia are adjacent to each other, and Zhangjiakou and Kulun are important passages to the Soviet Union. Recently, the re-establishment of diplomatic relations between China and the Soviet Union has become a reality. Even if a military alliance is not yet the time, it will not be difficult for China and the Soviet Union to reach further understanding if there is a war between Japan and the two countries. However, since Japan is bound to dominate maritime transport in the Western Pacific, the safety of maritime traffic between China and the Soviet Union cannot be guaranteed. The most important route is the Zhang-Ku passage. Therefore, Japan is eager to attack Zhangjiakou to cut off the land connection between China and the Soviet Union.

Third, the Northwest has a vast land with sparse population, rich products, simple customs, and abundant resources that are no less than those of the Northeast. The Wuyuan granary is the source of life for the provinces of Chahar, Suiyuan, Shaanxi, Gansu, and Shanxi. Japanese nationalists have long wanted to seize the life of our country's northern region. Therefore, they will extend their clutches and sweep Inner Mongolia to fulfill their dream of a Greater East Asia Monroe Doctrine.

These three points are enough to determine that Japan has long been determined to invade Zhangjiakou. Moreover, Zhangjiakou is the most important support point of the Ping-Sui Railway and is also related to Rehe. If our country truly wants to resist Japan, we must regard Zhangjiakou as the northern center and complete the railway from Datong to Shaanzhou as quickly as possible so that our arteries can be connected and we can use them conveniently, take advantage of the enemy's weaknesses, and use our strengths to deal with the enemy, and be able to defend the key points and not be taken advantage of by the enemy again. Then we can establish a foothold and plan an active counterattack. Therefore, today, whether we adopt a temporary defensive posture or an active counterattack, we cannot retreat any further in the territory of Hebei, and Duolun is the northern gateway lock, and Zhangjiakou is the support point of Ping Sui. We must do our best to maintain them. On the one hand, we should give full supplies to Sun Dianying's troops and others fighting on the front line so that they can do their best to fight guerrilla warfare to contain the enemy's forces. On the other hand, we should launch a large army to rectify the anti-Japanese steps, not only making the area between Duolun and Zhangjiakou a golden city for thousands of miles, but also build fortresses along the Shangdu River to Fengning, relying on the Wuling Mountains, to form mutually supporting positions with the Gubeikou garrison. If it is convenient, we can advance and take Le Ping to recover Chengde. Otherwise, we should defend ourselves firmly as a preparation for an active counterattack. Then there is still hope for salvation.

Gubeikou

Localized Fighting Occurs 10

Enemy Reinforcements Arrive with One Brigade

Japanese Troops Shell Near Xidaliang

(Beiping) On the Gubeikou front, our army is still deploying fortified defenses in its original positions. The enemy army recently transferred one brigade of troops from Chengde to Baimaguan, west of Gubeikou. The leading troops have already arrived. This afternoon, a localized battle occurred with a certain division of our army near Xidaliang. The enemy fired more than forty shells, and we returned fire. Our side has already transferred certain divisions to reinforce and strictly defend Gubeikou and the vicinity of Pinggu. (Special Dispatch, 28th)

(Beiping) Telegraph from Shixia Town reports that the enemy has increased their troops to one brigade at Gubeikou. Most of the enemy troops appear to be moving toward Dushikou, west of Gubeikou. Our army has made adequate preparations. The military affairs on our front are under the command of a certain person. (Special Dispatch, 28th)

(Beiping) Telephone report from Shixia Town indicates that although the enemy has increased its forces at Gubeikou, they have no intention of attacking south, as if they are afraid of our counterattack. Our army is still firmly defending Nantianmen, confronting the enemy. Frontline scouts report that the Japanese army outside Gubeikou has removed many supplies, showing signs of retreat. (Special Dispatch, 28th)

(Beiping) Telephone report from Shixia Town indicates that the enemy’s Takeshita Detachment, yesterday, led a light cavalry machine gun unit and about 300 infantrymen, and launched an attack on the slopes of Shalingkou. A fierce battle ensued with our defending troops. We urgently dispatched a certain regiment for reinforcement and surrounded the enemy. Subsequently, over a hundred Mongol cavalrymen outflanked our left flank at Simatai, and fierce fighting ensued. The enemy could not withstand the attack until around 10:00 PM yesterday and retreated. Our army tracked and pursued them to the southern slopes of Dongguan. The enemy suffered more than ten casualties, and we seized two machine guns. (Special Dispatch, 28th)

(Beiping) The situation on the Gubeikou front is suddenly tense. Certain divisions of our army have been ordered to leave Miyun and arrive at Gubeikou for reinforcement. Fierce fighting is expected in the coming days. (Special Dispatch, 28th)

North China Propaganda Corps

Organization Complete, Departing for Ping 11

(Nanjing) The Military Affairs Commission’s North China Propaganda Corps has been organized. Leader Liu Jianqun convened all the staff members on the 28th for a briefing, instructing them on the propaganda direction and encouraging them to work hard. The corps is scheduled to depart entirely on the 29th, first heading to Ping, then to various locations for work. (Central News Agency Dispatch, 28th)

Page 6

Situation Tense in Eastern Chahar

Japanese Troops Invade Fengning 12

Rumors of Japanese Plans to Create Puppet Mongolian State

(Nanjing) Military authorities received a telegram from Duolun stating that the situation in Eastern Chahar has recently become tense again. Japanese troops east of Chuizishan are attempting to infiltrate Chahar through mountain paths and are planning to create a puppet Mongolian state, with the three special districts of Suiyuan, Chahar, and Ningxia, which lie outside the Great Wall, as the territory of the puppet Mongolian state. They are adopting the same means as they used to create the puppet Manchurian state: after a military invasion, they will use traitors as puppets to call upon and incite the Mongols. Currently, our forces in the vicinity of Duolun and the western Chuizishan line are fully prepared. We will strike if the enemy comes, and there will be no problem in defending the Chahar territory. However, the Japanese bandits are getting more and more bold, so we must work together to find a way to resist them and maintain our territory. (Special Dispatch, 28th)

(Beiping) The Japanese army's Miyake Detachment invaded Fengning and made contact with the righteous army there. There are currently no traces of the enemy in Xinglong County. (Special Dispatch, 28th)

(Beiping) It is rumored that Tang Yulin has assembled troops, reaching 30,000 men, near Fengning, and is about to launch a counterattack towards Fengning and other places, acting in conjunction with Sun Dianying's troops. (Special Dispatch, 28th)

Record of an Inspection of the Lengkou Front Line 13

Shao Yuanchong and Others Comfort the Troops at the Front

Shang Zhen Reports on the Recent Military Situation

Our Military Positions Are Solid and Well-Organized

Fierce Battles Expected in a Week

(Tianjin) A reporter accompanied Shao Yuanchong, Lu Dangping, and others to inspect the front lines. They arrived in Kaiping at 2:30 PM on the 27th. Shang Zhen, the general commander of the Second Army Corps, welcomed them at the station and hosted a dinner. Shang reported on the anti-Japanese efforts at Lengkou. Shao immediately expressed his condolences and said that sacrificing for the nation and the country was a great honor. He quoted the late Premier Sun Yat-sen, saying, "Even if we cannot succeed, we should still strive for benevolence." He stated that resisting Japan was the best opportunity for armed comrades to achieve benevolence and would surely receive enthusiastic support from the entire nation. Shang told the reporter that after the loss of Chengde, the Northeast Army's morale was low, and they feared being surrounded, so they retreated in different directions. The Miyama detachment of the Nakamura unit of the enemy's 32nd Regiment, consisting of over 2,000 men, advanced in over a hundred tanks, armored vehicles, and trucks from the Lingyuan-Nanling area, charging wildly as if entering an uninhabited land. They then drove south from Dazhangzi and occupied Lengkou on the afternoon of the 4th of this month. Our army received orders to advance on the 5th and immediately dispatched the Huang Guanghua division, which marched urgently through the night. They recaptured Lengkou on the 6th and pursued the enemy twenty li, occupying the Madaogou position. Miyama then led his troops to attack Xifengkou and Gubeikou and later led his troops to attack Lengkou again, suffering heavy losses from our army's repeated night attacks. In the last five or six days, they have not dared to attack, only sending aircraft to harass us every morning, with the first reconnaissance, and two, three or four bombardments, each time with four aircraft dropping twenty to thirty bombs. There was a strong wind and rain on the 26th and 25th, and the front line was very quiet. The military telephone lines were broken and repaired on the night of the 27th. At 8 PM, Shang accompanied Shao and Lu in a special train to Luozhou, where they transferred to cars and went to the front line via Qian'an. At 2 AM on the 28th, they met with division commanders Huang Guanghua and Gao Hongwen, who both expressed their determination to sacrifice for the country. Huang told the reporter that the enemy planes were old-fashioned, and the villages in the area had been bombed miserably, with many casualties among the people, who had now all been evacuated. Our army suffered few casualties. We had anti-aircraft machine guns, which the enemy feared, flying at altitudes above 2,000 meters. On the morning of the 27th, using binoculars to observe the enemy planes, they were single-wing Junkers type, with machine guns in the front; this was the first time this was observed. A total of sixty bombs were dropped in Yaozhuangzi, Jianchangying, Tangzhangzi, and other places, each bomb weighing over 200 pounds, creating craters over ten feet deep upon impact. The enemy had about twenty cannons, which they fired at our side from time to time. According to intelligence, the enemy has requested reinforcements and heavy artillery from the rear, predicting that there will be fierce battles in a week. Shao delivered words of consolation, as before. Lu said that the Beijing Local Autonomy Guidance Committee had raised a lot of funds and asked what the front lines needed to purchase. Huang said they needed shoes, socks, broadswords, cars, and hospital beds, and Lu promised to take care of it upon returning to Beijing. At 4 AM, they arrived at Lengkou by car and then walked six or seven li outside the pass to inspect the positions, which were exceptionally solid and well-organized. At dawn, the rumbling sound of cannons entered their ears, and they learned that the enemy was firing from Xiaojiadian, but our side did not respond. At 6:30 AM, they returned to Lengkou by car and returned to Luozhou. At 10 AM, they arrived in Kaiping. At noon, Shang requested Shao to give instructions and encouragement to the officers and generals under his command on the value of sacrificing for the country. At 7 PM, they arrived in Tianjin, and Shao scheduled to go to Beijing on the morning of the 29th to give lectures at various universities before returning to Nanjing. (Special dispatch on the 28th)

The Question of the Premier of the Executive Yuan 14

A Concrete Decision Will Be Made Today by the Central Political Council

Wang Jingwei Has Agreed to Resume His Post

(Nanjing) Since Premier Wang and Chairman Jiang met and conferred in Nanjing, Wang's resumption of his post as Premier of the Executive Yuan has become a non-issue. Neither Wang nor Song attended the Executive Yuan meeting on the 28th because Wang has not yet resumed his post, and Song has already resigned. The matter of resumption of the post will be decided by the Central Political Council on the 29th, or some say it will be decided by the Central Standing Committee on the 30th. Jiang visited Wang again at 6 PM on the 28th for further talks. In short, the matter will be resolved within days. (Central News Agency dispatch on the 28th)

(Nanjing) Chen Gongbo told reporters on the morning of the 28th that Wang has agreed to resume his post, pending a decision by the Central Standing Committee on the 30th. Chu Minyi said that Premier Wang, seeing the increasingly dangerous national situation and after repeated urging from various parties, has no reason to decline the resumption of his post. According to another person close to Wang, Wang has been consulting with the Central Government for days, focusing on rectifying domestic affairs and foreign policy, and is no longer insistent on resigning. However, when Wang left the country, the Central Government only approved a leave of absence. If he returns to work after the leave, only a report will be submitted to the Central Political Council or the Central Standing Committee. (Central News Agency dispatch on the 28th)

(Nanjing) Li Liejun visited Jiang and Wang on the morning of the 28th and made some suggestions on improving domestic affairs. (Special dispatch on the 28th)

(Nanjing) Jiang went to Wang's residence at the Railway Ministry on the morning of the 28th and talked for an hour before leaving. At 10:30 AM, Wang, Song Ziwen, Luo Wengan, and others went to Jiang's residence on Huangpu Road to discuss important government affairs. It is said that they also had thorough discussions on the diplomatic policies to be adopted by our country after Japan's withdrawal from the League of Nations. (Special dispatch on the 28th)

(Nanjing) Song Ziwen will take the night train to Shanghai tonight. (Special dispatch on the 28th)

(Nanjing) Wang Jingwei recently telegraphed Yu Youren, saying, "Comrades have been meeting and discussing for days, and matters are pending resolution. Please return to Nanjing immediately for a meeting." (Special dispatch on the 28th)

(Nanjing) Chen Gongbo said that Wang Jingwei has agreed to resume his post and will preside over the next week's Executive Yuan meeting. Last month, I planned to go to Rehe and Luozhou to inspect public organizations and the state of industry, but Rehe fell, and the situation became tense, so it was suspended indefinitely. Recently, the soldiers at the front have been bravely resisting Japan. I intend to go north at the beginning of next month to see the situation at the front, offer comfort, and inspect the state of industry in North China. If I am held back by departmental affairs, I should be able to set off before the 10th at the latest. (Special dispatch on the 28th)

Military Commission Appoints

Feng Zhanhai as Army Commander 15

(Beijing) The Military Commission recently appointed Feng Zhanhai as the commander of a certain army. Feng has already taken office at the defense post and has established an office in Beijing. (Special dispatch on the 28th)

Japanese Planes Drop Bombs North of Changli

Destroy American Missionary Residence 16

(Beijing) It is reported that the Japanese Legation received a document from the American Legation today, stating that on March 24, an airplane flew to Shetouying, six miles south of the Great Wall and due north of Changli, and dropped a bomb that exploded near the residence of the American missionary, Gao Du. Shortly after, another bomb was dropped next to his residence. Although Mr. and Mrs. Gao Du were not injured, their residence and courtyard were destroyed by the two bombs. The Japanese Legation has now forwarded this document to the Commander of the Kwantung Army. (Reuters dispatch on the 28th)

Japan Worries About Economic Blockade 17

Japanese Naval Authorities Observe and Take Precautions

League of Nations Secretary-General's Reply Arrives in Tokyo

(Tokyo) This morning, League of Nations Secretary-General Drummond sent the following reply to the Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs regarding the notification of withdrawal from the League of Nations sent by the Imperial Government yesterday. The reply especially quoted the full text of Article 1, Paragraph 3, of the Covenant, so it is worth noting whether there are any underlying implications. (Reply) To His Excellency Foreign Minister Uchida: This Secretary-General has received the telegram from your Excellency of the 27th. In the conclusion of your telegram, the Japanese Government, in accordance with the provisions of Article 1, Paragraph 3, of the Covenant, notifies the intention of Japan to withdraw from the League of Nations. Article 1, Paragraph 3, states that "A Member of the League may, after two years’ notice of its intention so to do, withdraw from the League, provided that all its international obligations and all its obligations under this Covenant shall have been fulfilled at the time of its withdrawal." This Secretary-General will immediately transmit this reply and your telegram to the member states. Drummond. (Dentsu dispatch on the 28th)

(Tokyo) Since receiving Japan's official notification of withdrawal, the League of Nations has convened an advisory committee, apparently to decide on a course of action. The naval high command generally holds the following observations: Although the League of Nations is not familiar with the situation in the Far East, it will not be swayed by the instigation of small countries to impose an economic blockade under Article 16 of the Covenant. However, the possibility of economic pressure under Article 10 or 11 of the Covenant cannot be ruled out. The most important thing to pay attention to is the embargo on weapons to both China and Japan, which is a possibility. If it is a narrow embargo on weapons, Japan currently imports only about 2 million in gold from Germany, the UK, and Belgium, while China imports 15 million in gold from the UK, the US, and France. Therefore, the countries that will find it difficult are the UK, the US, and France, which trade with China, while it will be irrelevant to Japan. However, the most important thing to be wary of is the embargo on weapons interpreted in a broad sense. If cotton and other military supplies are included, it will be a disguised form of economic pressure, which is essentially the same as the economic sanctions under Article 16. Therefore, depending on how things develop, it may provoke a dispute, and this is the most important point to be wary of. (Dentsu dispatch on the 28th)

British, French, and German Public Opinion 18

(London) The Times said in an editorial today, "The impact of Japan's withdrawal from the League of Nations will only be felt gradually in the future, as Japan's withdrawal will not take effect for two years under the law. However, the League's power in the Far East will be weakened as a result. Japan's cooperation seems to cease whenever there is a possibility that its country may suffer temporary disadvantage. Japan has already notified the League that it intends to increase its military equipment rather than reduce it, and that it wants to have a freer hand in China. Even if Japan's claim that China is not an organized country and therefore Japan cannot maintain normal relations with China is not fabricated, it is for this reason that the powers concerned must not interfere in China for their own benefit. In the future, the mutual trust between Japan and other countries that have signed the Nine-Power Treaty and the Kellogg-Briand Pact will naturally be interrupted, and the nature of the League will become more European as an indirect result of Japan's withdrawal."

The Daily Telegraph said, "The League of Nations will feel increasingly incomplete due to the withdrawal of the strongest country in the Far East. In legal terms, Japan has violated the League's rules. There are now various suggestions in Geneva regarding Japan's withdrawal, but economic resistance and arms embargoes, or empty talk of reclaiming the trusteeship of the South Pacific islands, will not help and will only increase unnecessary hatred. It is not too late for the League of Nations to discuss this issue again when it is formally raised."

The Daily Express said, "Japan cannot make its illegal actions legal by sending a telegram to Geneva, and the League of Nations cannot reduce its responsibility to China because of a telegram from Japan."

The News Chronicle said, "Past experience makes it unnecessary to attach importance to Japan's self-proclaimed efforts for peace. The League of Nations, with the close cooperation of the US and Russia, must find a way to maintain peace in Liaodong." (Reuters dispatch on the 28th)

(Paris) Le Journal of Paris commented on Japan's withdrawal today, saying that the League of Nations is now suffering from immature universalism, but the forced withdrawal of the only major Asian country that has adopted Western customs and methods is a strange way to remedy a defect. It also said that what has been lost due to past events is not Japan. (Reuters dispatch on the 28th)

(Berlin) After Japan's withdrawal from the League of Nations, German semi-official sources believe that the League of Nations should not be disappointed by this, saying that although Japan has announced its withdrawal, it must continue to bear the obligations of a member state for two years. During this period, the dispute between the League of Nations and Japan is certainly not absolutely impossible to resolve. (Havas dispatch on the 27th)

Saito Seeks Comprehensive Measures 19

(Tokyo) After the adjournment of yesterday's emergency cabinet meeting regarding the withdrawal from the League, Prime Minister Saito spoke of his feelings, saying, "I am filled with fear upon receiving the imperial rescript regarding the withdrawal. From now on, the government and the people must work together to ensure that the diplomatic policy after the withdrawal is based on world peace and the happiness of the people. However, concrete measures cannot be clearly stated today, as the international political situation is subtle. I urge the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to seek comprehensive measures. The day before yesterday, I met with Finance Minister Takahashi to discuss matters related to the closing of the Diet. I still intend to take charge of the current situation and have no intention of resigning. I also intend to visit Prince Saionji as soon as possible to report in detail on the political situation up to today. The theory of the return to constitutional rule is recently rampant among political parties, which is what I hope for. However, in order to achieve this, the political parties must first revitalize themselves and gain the trust of the people." (Dentsu dispatch on the 28th)

(Tokyo) It is generally believed that the current cabinet will collapse after the end of the Diet, but Prime Minister Saito believes that the extraordinary situation has not yet been resolved, and he seems to have decided to continue in office. He will disclose this decision when he visits Prince Saionji at the beginning of next month and at the local officials' conference. Therefore, the political situation may temporarily remain as it is. (Dentsu dispatch on the 28th)

Uchida Hopes for Understanding from the Powers 20

(Tokyo) Foreign Minister Uchida told reporters today regarding Japan's withdrawal from the League of Nations that other powers should understand that Japan had no choice but to do so, and that Japan's legitimate attitude towards China and Manchuria should be understood, otherwise unfortunate events would occur and hinder world peace. All political party leaders now support the government's actions. Seiyukai President Suzuki said that after Japan's withdrawal from the League of Nations, it must pursue an active diplomatic policy that asserts its own claims. Minseito President Wakatsuki said that the whole country should unite to fulfill its mission. Adachi, chairman of the Kokumin Domeikai, said that Japan should organize a League of Asia. (Reuters dispatch on the 28th)

(Tokyo) After sending the notification of withdrawal from the League of Nations, Foreign Minister Uchida made a statement to the press, saying that the process of the Japanese government's withdrawal from the League of Nations is now clear, and that any person in charge would have done the same. However, the situation from now on will not be so simple. First, the major issue of China is imminent, and its future cannot proceed as usual. We must have the cooperation of the entire nation, especially the support of the press. (Dentsu dispatch on the 28th)

(Tokyo) Regarding Japan's position vis-à-vis the League of Nations after the withdrawal, League of Nations Secretary-General Drummond interpreted the text of Article 1, Paragraph 3 of the Covenant, and sent a reply that gave the impression that Japan would retain its rights and obligations for the next two years. However, the view of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs is that the notification of withdrawal is a matter of substance rather than theory. Therefore, the effect of the withdrawal will occur immediately. However, the notification of withdrawal means political disengagement from the League of Nations. Therefore, Japan will only fulfill the formal obligation of contributing to expenses and will not comply with other obligations, but the obligation to comply with the Kellogg-Briand Pact remains unchanged. Therefore, Japan will not participate in the League Council but will only cooperate in peaceful endeavors that do not violate the above policy. (Dentsu dispatch on the 28th)

Takahashi Discusses Economic Blockade 21

(Tokyo) Finance Minister Takahashi, who completed the Diet battle and signed the imperial rescript on withdrawal from the League of Nations, met with a Dentsu reporter with great urgency, first denying rumors of his resignation, and then speaking freely about the current situation, saying that the economic blockade theory is absolutely out of the question. He said in essence, "Although there are widespread rumors that I will resign, I do not care. I am carefully considering the reorganization of the tax system and finances for the future. However, it is difficult to raise taxes after all. The only thing that may be raised in 1934 is the postal rate. Some say that since Japan has withdrawn from the League of Nations, other countries of the League of Nations will impose an economic blockade on Japan, but the world situation is not so easy. Even if there is an economic blockade, the one who will suffer will not be Japan, but foreign countries. Although the Diet is over, there are still many important tasks to be done, and I cannot go to Hayama for rest. This is a time when the whole country must unite and work hard." (Dentsu dispatch on the 28th)

Page 7

Setback in US-Soviet Resumption of Relations 22

Pittman States That Russian Debt Should Be Resolved Before Recognition

A Commercial Agreement Must Be Concluded Before Diplomatic Relations Can Be Restored

(Washington) In view of the statement issued today by Senator Pittman, Chairman of the Senate Foreign Relations Committee, the resumption of US-Soviet relations may be delayed. Pittman stated that he believes that the Russian debt issue should be settled before recognition. He also said that he believes that recognition of Soviet Russia should be based on a trade agreement. A trade agreement must be concluded before diplomatic relations can be restored. He meant that it would be too hasty for the President to simply appoint an ambassador and have the Senate approve it. An understanding must be reached on the main points of the existing issues before diplomatic relations can be restored. It is now reported that President Roosevelt has completed his study of the issue of recognizing Soviet Russia and will probably submit a formal special message to Congress after the rural relief bill and the unemployment relief bill are passed. (Kuomin News Agency dispatch on the 27th)

The United States and the Yellow Peril

Matsuoka's Trick to Alienate American Hearts 23

Japan Is Not Yet Qualified to Wage War Against the United States

And Uses the Purchase of American Goods to Win Over the United States

Roosevelt and Hull Receive Matsuoka on Friday

(New York) After the local World Telegram asked Japanese representative to the League of Nations Matsuoka Yosuke to frankly express his views on the interests of the United States and Japan in the Far East, Matsuoka published an article in that newspaper today, declaring that Japan's concern about the threat of the United States in the Far East is the same as the United States' concern about the Yellow Peril. However, Japan currently has no territory or fortresses in the American oceans, while the United States has territory in the Far Eastern oceans. Japan has never been a threat to American interests. Western people have always known that Japan is not yet qualified to wage war against the richest and safest country in the world. Matsuoka then made it clear that the Japanese were unable to believe that the United States had the other-regardingness that it often claimed in its Far Eastern interests, and that, on the whole, the Japanese were unable to agree that the United States' Far Eastern interests were based on maintaining the Kellogg-Briand Pact and the Nine-Power Treaty. The purchasing power of the 450 million Chinese people envisioned by the Americans is a dream. Most of the Chinese people are poor and how can they buy huge amounts of American goods? On the contrary, Japan buys more American goods than all the other places in the Far East combined. He greatly denigrated China's ability, and again discussed the dignity of treaties and the attitude of the United States towards Japan's military actions in Manchuria, and again argued that it was extremely difficult for the Japanese to understand why the Americans attached so much importance to Japan's adherence to the letter of the treaties, while the Europeans could be relaxed. It is also difficult to understand why the Americans pay so much attention to the morality of Manchuria, even more than to Chicago. (Kuomin News Agency dispatch on the 27th)

(Washington) US President Roosevelt and Secretary of State Hull have agreed to receive Matsuoka Yosuke at noon on Friday. The Japanese Embassy has notified Matsuoka that the time will be around noon, and it is expected that he will be treated to a luncheon. (Kuomin News Agency dispatch on the 28th)

Caused by Japanese Rumors

Soviet Red Army's Indignation 24

(Moscow) The local newspaper published a telegram received by Voroshilov from the Great Uli Red Army, in which the telegram declared the recent rumors of the rebellion of the Great Uli Red Army. According to reports, we learned that foreign newspapers published a message from a Japanese stating that the 55th Regiment of the Red Army in Great Uli had rebelled. There is no 55th Regiment here. The message is malicious incitement and rumor. Please convey to the person who created this message that we know the intention of this rumor, which is to deceive the people of the capitalist countries and say that the Soviet Union is weak, and its people are dissatisfied, so that it will be easier to prepare to attack the Soviet Union. There was a similar rumor in the Central East Road area in 1929, but the result was a failure. We are now even stronger, and they should remember that since the overthrow of the Tsar in 1917, we have been prepared to fight to the last drop of blood, so all rumors are useless. (TASS dispatch on the 27th)

Executive Yuan Meeting Yesterday 25

Lengthy Discussion on the Land Rent Issue

(Nanjing) At the Executive Yuan meeting on the 28th, the issue of land rent proposed by the Ministry of the Interior was discussed for a long time. The land rent issue is extremely complex, and the situations in the provinces and counties are different. An appropriate method that is not biased towards landowners or tenants should be determined according to local conditions. The 37.5% system that was previously implemented will be changed. It is said that the military unification proposal made by Commissioners Yu and Sun will be discussed at the Central Political Council on the 29th, and the content of the proposal focuses on wartime organization to facilitate the deployment and command of the troops fighting at the front. (Special dispatch on the 28th)

(Nanjing) The Executive Yuan held its 93rd meeting on the 28th. Gu Mengyu, Chen Shuren, Chen Shaokuan, Zhu Jiahua, Chen Gongbo, Liu Ruiheng, and Shi Qingyang attended. Guo Chuntao, Gan Naikang, Chen Yi, Xu Mo, Zou Lin, Zheng Tianxi, Shi Ying, Duan Xipeng, Chu Minyi, and Peng Xuepei were present as observers. Zhu Jiahua chaired the meeting. It is proposed to approve the resignation, and Pang Cheng, deputy brigade commander of the brigade, is proposed to be promoted to fill the vacancy.

(5) Approved: Minister He of the Military Affairs Commission reports that Feng 　, commander of the 239th Brigade of the Eightieth Division, has resigned. It is proposed to approve the resignation, and Chen Qi is proposed to fill the position.

(6) Approved: Minister He of the Military Affairs Commission requests that Cha Guangbi be appointed as the chief of the general affairs section of the Shanghai Steel Smelting Plant, and Li Liyan be appointed as the chief of the engineering section of the plant.

(7) Approved: Minister Song of the Ministry of Finance reports that Fang　xian, director of the Anhui Province Stamp Tax Bureau, Luo Shoupeng, deputy director of the Hubei Province Stamp Tax Bureau, and Cao Mingxian, deputy director of the Jiangxi Province Stamp Tax Bureau, have other appointments. Li Wuchen, director of the Shandong Province Stamp Tax Bureau, has been dismissed for a case. Zheng Hui, deputy director of the Fujian Province Stamp Tax Bureau, and Shen Zongqian, deputy director of the Jiangsu Province Stamp Tax Bureau, are awaiting other appointments. It is also requested that Liang Jiagan be appointed as the director of the Anhui Province Stamp Tax Bureau, Chen Xizhi be appointed as the director of the Jiangxi Province Stamp Tax Bureau, Zhou Zongyao be appointed as the director of the Shandong Province Stamp Tax Bureau, Luo Shoupeng be appointed as the deputy director of the Jiangsu Province Stamp Tax Bureau, Cao Mingxian be appointed as the deputy director of the Hubei Province Stamp Tax Bureau, and Xu Xian be appointed as the deputy director of the Fujian Province Stamp Tax Bureau.

It is requested that they be dismissed, and Bai Fengzhao, Wang Huimin, Wang Yun, and O Qiguang are appointed to fill the vacancies.

Japanese Atrocities in Shenyang 26

Testimony from Righteous Army Commander Zhao Dianliang

(Beiping) Righteous Army Commander Zhao Dianliang came to Beiping and spoke of the extreme cruelty of the Japanese in Shenyang since the outbreak of the Rehe War. They forcibly seize carts and conscript laborers. In every village in the countryside, they demand ten carts. Before the conscripted civilians and carts even set out, two men are handcuffed together. After departure, they are chained to the carts to prevent escape. The carts are filled with sandbags to shield the Japanese soldiers as they drive them to the front lines, resulting in a great number of carters dying. Their bodies are continuously transported to the South Manchurian Railway station in Shenyang, three corpses tied together, and notices are posted for families to claim them. There are very few Japanese troops in the city, only around 800. Fearing unrest in the rear, they display their strength with tanks. Police substations have each been reduced by eighty officers. Civilian firearms in Fushun, Tieling, Faku, Xinmin, Liaozhong, Liaoyang, and other counties have all been ordered to be surrendered. To protect their weapons, many people have joined the Righteous Army. Therefore, the authorities have recently become less strict about confiscating arms. Many members of the Jing'an Guerrilla Force have been deployed to the Rehe front lines, with over six hundred deserting en route. Furthermore, the Japanese army has been recruiting bandits from various regions and arresting loiterers in theaters and brothels. (28th Dispatch)

Over Ten Die of Illness in Beiping 27

Due to Abnormally Squalid Living Conditions

Seven Thousand Righteous Soldiers Leave Russia

(Beiping) Over a thousand family members of Su, Ma, Li, and Wang, as well as civilians from the Northeast, returned from Soviet Russia and resided in the New World Building. Due to the cramped space and abnormal squalor, over ten people have died from infectious diseases in recent days. The Support Association has sent a letter to the Public Security Bureau, requesting assistance in finding alternative housing to prevent further infections. (28th Dispatch)

Furthermore, it is reported that seven thousand members of the volunteer army recently departed from Tomsk in Russia, arrived in Dihua, and will return to Beiping via Gansu, Ningxia, and Zhangjiakou. Jiangsu Province Divided into Thirteen Districts

Administrative Inspectorates Established 46

Commissioner of Each District Announced

Changes to County Magistrates in Various Counties

(Zhenjiang) The Jiangsu Provincial Government believes that Jiangsu, bordering the sea and the Yangtze River, is strategically important. Faced with the current severe national crisis and complex administration, it has followed the central government's system of administrative inspectorates and the regulations of the provinces of Henan, Hubei, and Anhui, taking into consideration the actual needs of the province. Soviet Representative Criticizes

British Disarmament Plan 53

Military Figures Only Reflect Europe

The Number of Japanese Standing Army Cannot Be Ignored

Russia’s Neighboring Countries Would Increase Military Strength

TASS, Geneva, 27th: Soviet representative Dovgalevsky delivered a lengthy speech in the General Committee of the Disarmament Conference today, sharply criticizing the disarmament plan proposed by British Prime Minister MacDonald. MacDonald believes that one of the characteristics of the British disarmament plan is that it contains specific figures for disarmament. On this point, Dovgalevsky pointed out that the Soviet Union had already listed specific and accurate figures in its first proposal for complete and universal disarmament and its second proposal for gradual proportional disarmament. Dovgalevsky believes that the British plan has two shortcomings: (1) More than fifty countries attended the Disarmament Conference, but the military figures cited by Britain only reflect European countries, and only a part of European countries. (2) The British Prime Minister did not explain the basis of the standard for his figures. Dovgalevsky said that the Soviet delegation should first declare that the Soviet Union is very willing to reduce the number of its standing army to below the level of the British plan, but it always requires that this proportion must be applied to all countries, without exception, whether in Europe or outside Europe. At the same time, the Soviet Union is also willing to make a large reduction in the quality of armaments according to the British plan. The Soviet Union believes that Britain should explain the basis of the standard for the disarmament figures it has set, and this standard should be used to stipulate the disarmament figures for countries not included in the plan. Regarding the number of standing troops of the Soviet Union’s Asian neighbors, such as Japan, the Soviet representative believes that it cannot be ignored, and the territory that can be armed by the country on the border should also be considered. In addition, the British plan stipulates that Norway’s standing army should be 50,000, but according to the Norwegian representative, this number exceeds the country’s existing military strength. Then the question is whether the Soviet Union’s western neighbors, that is, what the plan calls “all other European countries,” should be allowed to increase their armaments because of the British plan. Dovgalevsky also declared that the Soviet Union supports the principle of drastically reducing the length of military service, but believes that the implementation of this reduction should include all countries, including all colonies. Regarding the part on air force reduction, Dovgalevsky declared that the Soviet representative wants to know the basis of the calculations made in the British plan. The Soviet Union believes that air force reduction should be universal to all countries participating in the conference, which is an absolute necessity, especially since the Soviet Union’s neighbors, such as Japan’s air force, have recently established military aviation teams outside its borders. Dovgalevsky also criticized the part of the British plan that retains the allowance for air force bombing, believing that it must be changed to a complete abolition of bombing from the sky. Finally, regarding naval disarmament, Dovgalevsky explained that the Soviet Union did not participate in the Washington and London Naval Treaties, so it cannot be required to unconditionally obey such regulations. As for the principle of naval reduction proposed in the British plan, the Soviet Union believes that what should be considered is that it divides all countries into two levels, one that should maintain the current state of the navy, and one that should be allowed to increase it.

Disarmament Recesses for One Month 54

National Geneva Dispatch, 27th: The General Committee of the Disarmament Conference has now adjourned until April 27. Many representatives expressed the hope that the four major European powers will be able to reach some special understanding during this period based on the proposal made by British Prime Minister MacDonald. Before the adjournment, the General Committee had a resolution specifying that after Easter, the British proposal would be used as the basis for discussion. This proposal was made by British Foreign Secretary Simon, who stated that representatives should retain the right to propose modifications and additions. Also, before the representatives boarded their cars to return home, a majority of representatives stated that they hoped that Britain, France, Italy, and Germany could reach some understanding during the recess. If no understanding can be reached, some representatives advocate an indefinite recess, frankly admitting that the General Committee has failed. However, these people believe that the British proposal can be the basis for direct negotiations between the four countries and can achieve some agreement.

Hitler's Party and

Steel Helmet League Breaks Up 56

Organization Dissolved, Over a Thousand Arrested

National News, Brunswick, 28th - Last night, the Brunswick Steel Helmet League organization was forcibly dissolved, members disarmed, and 1,350 people arrested, causing great shock among the populace. According to a public statement by Class, National Socialist member and Brunswick State Interior Minister, in recent days, a significant number of Social Democrats and Communists had joined the Steel Helmet League. Moega, leader of the Brunswick Steel Helmet League, acknowledged that members of the disbanded Republican Flag League and other Republican groups had been flocking to the Steel Helmet League headquarters to register, and armed Steel Helmet League members, belonging to the auxiliary police, were providing protection along the way, shouting their unit's battle cry. Last night, regular police, acting on orders from the Brunswick State government and assisted by National Socialist stormtroopers, searched for Steel Helmet League members who had joined the auxiliary police and surrounded the Steel Helmet League's office where a meeting was in progress, arresting 200 Steel Helmet League members and 1,150 Social Democrats and Communists inside, including several leaders of the Steel Helmet League and the Republican Flag League. During the encirclement, several auxiliary police members belonging to the Steel Helmet League reportedly destroyed their rifles.

National News, Berlin, 28th - Labor Minister and Steel Helmet League leader Serld has begun a thorough investigation of the Brunswick State government's handling of the Steel Helmet League case. Today, Seton met with National Socialist cabinet member Goering for a long discussion and also met with Interior Minister Dr. Frick. It is rumored that Steel Helmet League leaders will issue a statement today, which, according to key figures in the League, will differ greatly from the Brunswick State Interior Minister's account. The Brunswick State government is now in a difficult position, as it is unsure how to handle such a large number of arrestees, as individual trials would take a very long time.

Feng Sends Letter to Chiang Kai-shek 57

Offers Five Suggestions for Resisting Japan

After Feng Yuxiang retired to Zhangjiakou, Chairman Chiang sent Ma Boyuan to Zhang to discuss everything and urged Feng to come to Nanjing. Feng expressed his willingness and replied to Chiang with a letter offering five suggestions for resisting Japan. The original letter is recorded as follows: "Elder Brother Kai-shek, Upon receiving your telegram and Ma Boyuan's visit to Zhang, I am deeply moved by your kindness. The country is in peril, and only sincere unity and concerted efforts to seek solutions can save us. I, Xiang, share weal and woe, life and death with you, my brother, to complete the Northern Expedition. Our personal friendship remains as it was. Even if our opinions sometimes differ, they arise from a desire to create a new nation. Now, the national crisis deepens daily, and the enemy continues to advance. This is truly a time of greatest danger. We must strive to defend ourselves and resist desperately to avert destruction. I have several points to present to you: (1) Rumors of compromise are widespread at home and abroad. These are certainly created by the enemy. However, our way to dispel these rumors must be through factual counter-evidence, then the rumors will cease naturally. Please pay attention to this. (2) Quickly dispatch elite troops from all sides, so that resistance is not limited to one corner. I especially hope that you, my brother, will personally lead one hundred thousand troops to recover lost territory. I will do my utmost to assist. (3) The troops fighting hard against the enemy at the front are extremely short of supplies and ammunition. Please find a way to replenish them. (4) The anti-Japanese armies and militias have suffered heavy casualties. Please find a way to provide relief and replenishment. (5) Politics is the foundation of everything. I especially hope that the government will reform and start anew with the people. The above five points are my humble suggestions. I hope you will adopt them. For anything unsaid, please ask Comrade Xiwen to convey it in person. Sincerely, Younger Brother Feng Yuxiang."

He Zhuguo Speaks

Situation on the Ledong Front 58

Summoned to Ping from Defense Zone

Completed Troop Rotation with a Certain Unit

His Troops Still on the Front Line

Beiping Correspondence: He Zhuguo, who commands troops stationed in Ledong, received an order from the Military Council on the 17th to rotate troops with the XX unit. He's unit had gradually concentrated by the previous day (24th). Chairman Chiang and Minister He, in order to understand the recent situation in Ledong, specially telegraphed and summoned He to Ping. General He left Lixian by special train at 6 PM the previous night, passed through Tianjin that night, and met with Chairman Yu Xuezhong to discuss matters of joint defense. He arrived in Ping at 8 AM yesterday (25th) and went to Jurentang at 7 PM that evening to meet with Minister He to report on the troop rotation in Ledong. Originally intending to visit Chiang in Baoding, he found Chiang had already left, so he scheduled to return to his defense zone at 6 PM today (26th). According to a statement made by He:

Strategic Relations 59

Since the Jehol Incident, the Japanese army has been using threatening tactics against various parts of Ledong. On one hand, they increased troops in Yuguan and attacked nearby ports, and on the other hand, they deployed a large number of warships and anchored in Qinhuangdao to exert pressure by land and sea. The highest military authorities, considering that our army's garrison in Linyu had become a militarily exposed situation, ordered a troop rotation on the 17th of this month for strategic reasons, to be filled by troops stationed in a certain unit's position. Extremely solid trenches have been built on the Shi River and nearby front lines. The troops currently rotating have also arrived. There has been much speculation about our unit from the outside, but it is all talk without knowing the truth.

Still on the Front Line 60

Since the September 18th Incident, Yuguan has been under the enemy's covetous eyes, with danger at every turn. I have been stationed in Yuguan for a year and three months. During this period, the Japanese army's conspiracies and attempts to invade have been more than one or two days. On January 1st, the enemy launched a large-scale land, sea, and air offensive, and our army retreated to the west bank of the Shi River. In these several months, we resisted the enemy, deeply desiring to sacrifice everything, but lacking orders. Since then, although our troops have been in Lixian, they are still on the front line. If the enemy invades, we swear to fight with the entire army.

Japanese Attack Six Ports 61

The Japanese army invading Jehol, according to investigations, totals over 50,000, including a mixed force of Zhang Haipeng and other puppet troops, totaling about 100,000. In addition, the Yiyuan Kou and Jiumen Kou areas have the puppet "National Anti-Japanese Salvation Army" organized by Ding Qiang. The Japanese army's plan is to attack our six ports, namely Shanhaiguan, Jiumenkou, Jielingkou, Xifengkou, and Gubeikou. Currently, some have already been occupied by the Japanese army, and some are facing off. The Japanese steps to invade us are: (1) Shanhaiguan uses the Boxer Protocol as an excuse, but destroys the treaty and forcibly occupies our Yuguan land. (2) For Jehol, it occupies our Jehol province based on the unilaterally signed Japan-Manchukuo Protocol. (3) It uses the "Anti-Japanese Salvation Army" organized by puppet troops to harass our Yiyuan Kou, attempting to disrupt the interior. Currently, the Japanese army is not actively preparing for a military offensive on Ledong because the Japanese warships previously in the Qinhuangdao sea have gradually left, and there are only 300-400 garrison troops in Yuguan city.

Front Line Situation 62

Fangling Kou and Jieling Kou definitely had fierce battles yesterday. Commander Shang has personally gone to the front to supervise the battle. The enemy troops attacking Leng Kou are the 10th Division and part of the 14th Division's Hiraga Brigade, totaling about 3,000. Yesterday, they used extremely fierce artillery fire to press against us, but were all repelled by Huang's troops. There were also battles at Jieling Kou, where Miao's entire division is responsible for that line. The battle on the Yiyuan Kou side seems to have passed. Recently, the enemy army transferred the puppet troops of Zhang Haipeng and Yu Zhishan to the Daling River Bridge, where they were suddenly disarmed by the Japanese army. The Japanese army has always considered the various puppet troops to be unreliable, and the puppet army generals, suffering this unexpected blow, all plan to hang the Blue Sky White Sun flag and are unwilling to submit to the Japanese army. (26th)

Sends Special Telegram to Nanjing Vowing to Sacrifice Lives to Repay the Country

Overseas Chinese Present Flags and Swords as Encouragement

Beijing News: Wu Qiwai, commander of the Army's Fourth Army, has recently led his troops in suppressing bandits in Jiangxi and has repeatedly achieved remarkable feats. The army is known as the Iron Army for its loyalty, bravery, and skill in battle. At this time of growing national crisis and rising calls for resistance, the army's situation is of great concern to the people. When the wind is strong, one thinks of brave warriors. The Central Government previously transferred the army to Jiangxi to suppress bandits. In the end, the bandits were defeated, and the army was approved by the Central Government to accept the surrender of a division of communist bandits led by Guo, which was a great achievement. Chairman Chiang once sent a commendation. It is recently heard that all officers and soldiers of the army, in response to the loss of Yu and Rehe, telegraphed to request to go north to participate in the war against Japan and vow to sacrifice their lives to repay the country. It is unknown whether this request will be approved. Furthermore, overseas Chinese have always admired the army. The Boston branch of the KMT in the United States sent a letter of encouragement and presented General Wu with a command sword and a large flag. For the past ten years, your army has traveled throughout the Central Plains to protect the Party and save the country, enduring hardship and danger. Your heroic deeds have been admired. Even last year's request to go to Shanghai to fight against Japan, although unrealized, we believe the people understand the bitterness of not being able to reach the front lines. We, overseas, wholeheartedly support your army's efforts and greatly value your efforts to save the country and protect the party. Sincerely wishing you victory, The Chinese Nationalist Party's Boston Branch in the United States, Standing Committee Member Huang Qike, Chen Dunhong, Chicken Building Manager Yu Xue Li, Manager Yu Li Kun, February 14"

Robbery and Assault in Dong Yaojia Bang 64
